RATING: 6
Light silly game about gardening and eating with nice components and a small touch of strategy.

On a given turn, you roll the dice (this is not as bad as it sounds), which determines the "weather" which is to say it gives a special effect for that player- all the effects are good, such as an extra action, being able to duplicate an action etc., but they are not all necessarily balanced, and worse, they can be very situational (and not come up in the situation when you need them and vice versa).  On your turn, you typically have 2 actions, and they range from laying a tile (which expands the garden, and which is useful for potential scoring cards), move the gardener (which grows bamboo also useful for scoring cards), move the panda (who eats the bambo, useful for scoring cards), take a scoring card, and irrigate a tile (this action works similar to Santiago although it is a very weak action in this game).

The game ends when a player has completed a set number of scoring cards.  All points are gained through the scoring cards, with a small bonus for the first player to finish.

The game looks super light and fluffy, and to an extent it is, but it's still a good design with a bit of game in it, and the components/theme will be a definite plus for some people.

Own the [boardgame=174095]Chibis[/boardgame] expansion.

RATING: 4
Takenoko is a game by designer Antoine Bauza (a well-known designer who has also produced hits like Tokaido, 7 Wonders, and Hanabi. He has a thing for Japan, it seems). Takenoko packages fun, gorgeous artwork with a competitive tile-laying game. Much like Tokaido, this game is competitize in a lighter, more zen sense than other, more cutthroat games.

Together, players are moving the various tokens around (panda and gardener) to eat and plant bamboo shoots, that are grown on irrigated tiles that are also laid by the players. All players are competing for secret objectives that earn points. Everyone's objectives are different, so players will find themselves competing to get the panda and the tiles in the right positioning to achieve their own goals.

A fun little game that's light on rules and light on strategy; a nice (though frustrating for me) balance that will appeal to many people.

RATING: 6
Obviously this has a good theme - they ought to sell it at Edinburgh zoo now that they have the pandas as it may sell by the bucketload.  It's visually very interesting. Some of the play is a wee bit reminiscent of a stripped down Santiago.  It's not as clean and deep as that one by a long chalk, but it is a decent game.  The cards and tiles offer lots of luck.- you can draw pink bamboo on cards bu not on tiles for instance, which hampers you massively, but then I'm not one of those measly party-popping gamers who insists that every game needs to have minimum luck.  It's nice to have a bit of variety.

The more advanced rules would be beyond a lot of kids under ten on the first play as the game is a lot meatier than it's theme suggests or than you would expect in a "kids' game."  I think it's more of a family game really.

As a game I'd give it a 5, but since it's got a great theme is good, light fun and has wonderful bits I think a 6 is more reasonable.

RATING: 8
Unique modular board game with a colorful, happy theme. I've played 2p and 4p, and both games were interesting and entertaining. Great for families with younger kids (7+).

The components are wonderful, the mechanics make sense, and the player mats really aid in the fluidity of the game. With several paths to victory, you never feel like one strategy trumps all the others, and being able to play off of other player's decisions makes the game dynamic and unpredictable.

I really enjoy Takenoko, and I hope I get to play it more.

RATING: 7
A cool game.  Limited action selection with personal card-based goals (objectives).  And it has a panda.  Which is cool.  Really this is an abstract with a nice, friendly, cute theme pasted on.  But it works very well so it doesn't quite feel like an abstract and doesn't hit that oh-boy-this-is-dry point that most abstracts do.

Why not a higher score then?  Because the goal cards drive EVERYTHING.  You can draw into a HORRIBLE combination and be behind for the rest of the game.  Like I did.  And there's very little you can do to repair this if other players are able to capitalize on their goals.  Which they will.  Because they can.  And you can't.  And you must spend actions drawing MORE goal cards to fix the problem.

Oddly enough this is solved fairly easily (I suspect).  Draw 2, keep 1 for opening goal draws?  Draw 2, keep 1 for whole game?  Have a visible goal offer?

But it still leaves the problem of drawing into the perfect goal.  Mid-to-late game, your draw may yield a goal that is 1-action away while my draw yields an impossible goal (or one that would take far too much time or luck to accomplish).  There's something slightly wacky where good goal draws can overshadow someone else's superior play.  And that irks me.

Even so, the theme prevails and I would play this game at least until it annoys me enough to lower the rating and cry foul.

RATING: 7
FAVOURITE GAME - it is a stunningly beautiful entry level boardgame, where you control a gardener growing bamboo and a panda eating the bamboo. You have secret objectives cards which you have to fulfill to gain points (growing bamboo, eating bamboo, building a garden). The objectives are a bit unbalanced, as it is harder to grow bamboo than eating it, but the same points go for each, but still, it is a fun game, with easy rules and stunning visuals.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
An unusual and cute theme - a pet panda chomping its way through the Japanese Emperor's bamboo patch.  The production is quite endearing too, with panda and gardener figures and nicely done bamboo segments.

I wish the game we are given to play with this nice stuff were better.  Takenoko offers three ways to score; by collecting sets of eaten bamboo, by growing bamboo in specific locations, and by achieving various patterns of land tiles. Scoring cards are drawn in the manner of tickets in Ticket to Ride.  What you quickly learn is that eating sets of bamboo is the easiest thing to do in the early game.  In the late game, drawing land tile scoring cards can get you instant points for a pattern that already exists.  Whether you get easy points or something impossible to complete is all down to the luck of the draw.  Add the luck of a weather die roll, which randomly gives you an always useful extra action or some other effect that may be of no use.  Add the chaos of other players unwittingly contributing to or hindering completion of your secret objectives.

I found Takenoko quite painless and even a bit of fun to play. However, I don't think it is a very good game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A little gem of a game that's lighthearted and super easy to pick up and play.
The idea of the game is to accumulate points by completing objectives. The objectives are in 3 categories; Bamboo growth, Panda bamboo consumption, and land hex arrangement.
Land hexes and bamboo shoots are in 3 colours; pink, yellow and green. 
Completing bamboo growth cards involves using a combination of rain and the farmer to make bamboo of particular colours to grow to certain heights. Completing panda bamboo consumption cards means moving the panda to where bamboo is growing and eating the shoots (See how these 2 types work for and against each other). Finally the land placement objectives are met by placing land hexes of particular colours into given arrangements in the play area.

The artwork is lovely and playful and the pieces are very well made. I would recommend this as a way to get kids involved in games or for involving girlfriends that aren't really into heavy duty strategy games.

RATING: 7
Players: 2-4
Time: 45 mins

The players take the role of courtesans of the Nippon emperor. They take care of his Giant Panda by growing a bamboo plantation. Their mission: to farm parcels of land, irrigate them, and have green, yellow or pink bamboo grow. In turn, they see what the weather brings and perform two actions from among those offered to them: get a new plot of land or irrigation channel, grow bamboo, feed the panda or draw an objective card.

RATING: 7
Gran juego familiar, tiene los toques de azar y control indicados para gran diversión, no es un juego muy profundo, porque no es su objetivo.

Sin duda el mejor juego de menos de 1 hora que he jugado.

Logra ser inmersivo por su temática y la calidad excepcional de sus componentes, son una maravilla.

Funciona perfecto a 2 jugadores, un gran logro, realmente recomendado para comenzar ludoteca, más entretención a mi modo de ver que catan.

Nota: Los objetivos de parcelas dan pocos puntos, sin ser fácil realizarlos. Por lo que se recomienda agregar lo siguiente: Por cada set de 3 objetivos distintos cumplidos, se dan 3 puntos de victoria adicionales (set: objetivo de panda, granjero y parcela). Esto da incentivo a utilizar los objetivos de parcelas.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This game will either be a hit or a miss with a game group.  It's not really clear why, but I suspect it relates to the group dynamic and the player's ability to work with shared components.  In this game, the farmer and the panda are both shared elements in the game.  (For that matter, the board tiles and the bamboo are as well!)  And a player needs all of these to align in the right way to score points based on hidden objective cards.  If the other players 'don't cooperate' with your plans, you might not do so well.  But if you are flexible and adjust to the situation well, this game can be a great deal of light fun.  It will not be a brain-burner.  But it is not merely light fluff.  Observing and responding to the board's development is key.  If you miss this, it can feel chaotic.  If you get it, it will feel tactical.  Excellent components, visually appealing, and approachable (to some crowds) combine to make it a fine family game.

RATING: 7
An interesting but light game, with some interesting mechanisms, like the push and pull of farmer trying to grow the bamboo shots and the panda trying to eat them.

It's definitely a family game, with weather die randomly giving a player a bonus that lift some of the game's restrictions (i.e. one side allows a player to take three actions, not two; or take two of the same action) that makes it easier to do stuff. It can also be a bit lucky with objective cards, I feel like I jump from third to almost first with some lucky card draws on the last turn.

RATING: 6
Számomra ez abszolút Ticket to ride jellegű és szintű játék, ezért pontszámban is ugyanannyit adok rá. Talán a TTR letisztultabb, de ez meg egyedibb témájú, végre nem egy újabb vonatos célkártyás játék.
Ritkán mondok ilyet, de ez egy aranyos játék, sokkal inkább érzem családinak a bambuszt rágcsáló pandát, mint a vonatokat (nem is értem egyébként ezt a nagy vonatbuzulást a társasjátékok világában, azt elismerem, hogy vannak jó vonatos játékok, de magát a tényt nem értem, miért jelenik meg ennyi vonatos játék.) 
De visszatérve a pandákra: a nagy gondom a játékkal, hogy óriási szerencsefaktort jelentenek a célkártyák, mert egész könnyű kártyákat is lehet húzni, és nagyon nehezeket is, és a kártyák pontszáma szerintem nem mindig tükrözi a nehézségi szintet.
Egyébként a célkártyák többsége nagyon gyorsan teljesíthető, a pálya folyamatosan változik, ezért szigorúan taktikai játék, ritkák a körökön átívelő célok. Bár az lehet stratégiai döntés, hogy milyen típusú kártyákra megy rá valaki (külön vannak válogatva típusok szerint), ennek szabályozására különböző variánsok születtek, mi is egy ilyet próbáltunk (nem lehet a kézben 2 azonos típusú célkártya, ha nincs mindháromból legalább 1).
Összességében kellemes játék, nem korszakos, de néha szívesen játszom vele.

RATING: 6
First off, this game is beautiful.
The whole concept of growing this communal garden is fantastic, and there is something really zen about the whole process.

As much as I enjoy the concept and general game play. I often find I am craving some deeper strategy elements to this game. Maybe after a group has played it enough to know all the cards, and understand every option, it would be possible to play deeper. But for the moment, I find I don't have the capability to block my opponents, or even read them well enough to know what they are planning. As so many goal cards require all 3 elements to be utilised.

This game is still fun, and doesn't take an absurd amount of time. Just has the slight feeling of just going through the motions around the middle of the game.

Would recommend as a lighter/introductory game to newer table top players.

RATING: 6
The rating is for the Collector's Edition.

This is a wholesome light medium weight family game with a bit of randomness in regards to cards drawn and the outcome of the die. Still, it does hold your attention as a quick fun game and for the production values; especially the nicely done figures, the oversized die and tiles and the ton of wood that is bamboo. It also comes in a beautiful custom made box with foam inserts for the pieces.

There is a game in there for new gamers or family nights, but experienced gamers will probably bore quickly. Don't get me wrong, there are some decisions to be made and a layer of depth that appeared after a few plays, but the game felt that it would be scripted and repetetive after a few plays... In the few plays that I had, it seemed that some of the card objectives were a bit easier to accomplish than others, but I need to reasses to confirm. 

This will probably have a higher appeal to father/daughters, girlfriends/wives or smaller kids for the theme, cuteness factor and beautiful bits/colors. On the other spectrum, it will probably be highly sought after by collectors if the print run is limited.

RATING: 9
I can’t believe it, I’ve found an eurogame I actually like! And as though this weren’t surprising enough, I have to add I can’t even stand either Seven Wonders, the previous hit by the same author, and any Far Eastern theme!

There’s something charming in Takenoko indeed I still can’t point out even though I’ve played it quite a few times: I surely like the extreme simplicity and clarity of its rules but I also enjoy how everything plays smoothly and at the same time gives the game its strong thematic flavor.

On the other hand, it’s a pity the interaction among the players is minimal or nonexistent: nonetheless the game does neither suffer from the lacking of direct conflict (there’s enough to do to keep you busy) nor feel like a «multiplayer solitaire» like most euros do. (October 2012)

[b]Update[/b] - A year has passed since my first plays and I still can’t get Takenoko off my mind: it’s such a fun game!

Not only do I play it gladly every time the chance occurs but I also suggest it to any undecided gamer who asks for advice, insomuch that I’ve put it in my personal list of the best gateway games for everyone, as it’s both easy to grasp and play without being either shallow or childish though.

Undoubtedly, Takenoko’s strong point (and what won me over) is you don’t have to pointlessly grind points all over the game as in your typical euro but on the contrary your efforts are directed towards specific short-term goals shown on the cards you draw, for which reason in November 2013 I raised my rating from 8 to 9.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
Takenoko is a light and breezy game in which you get random objectives and then take 2 actions per turn of 5 available to complete them.  There is very little other players can do to stop or even slow you from completing objectives, so it turns into a race of who can complete their objectives fastest.  If this resulted in an efficiency contest, it would be a fine game.  But it doesn't.

The issue is that the bamboo comes in 3 colors, and there are different numbers of tiles for each color.  Green is most common, followed by Yellow, and Pink is rarest.   The points available for each objective scale with the rarity of the color, so having a Pink shoot 4 sections tall is worth much more than a Green one.  BUT - when placing tiles, players draw 3 and pick 1 to place.  Which, in practice, means that Pink tiles are almost as easy to come by as yellow and green.  The game would significantly benefit if the points were dependent on how rare the _Objective_ was, rather than how rare the tile was.  If there were fewer pink objectives, then fewer players would be incentivized to play pink, and then the higher point weighting would make sense.  As it is, if you draw pink objectives (and the color required to complete any given objective is random), then you will score more points and win, because the pink objectives will usually take you the same amount of actions to score them as yellow and green objectives.  

For this reason, I consider Takenoko to be a very sophisticated version of Candyland - most of the game is decided by what cards you draw.  It is a pleasant enough way to spend 30-45 minutes, and seems very suitable for kids.  But it is not a competitive activity, nor will it require you to think overmuch.

Sold.  I will only play again with kids, and only if they beg a little.

RATING: 8
This game is near and dear to my heart. Fun, strategic paper-rock-scissor dynamic. You can go for tile-playing, which can score lots of small, easy points. Or you can opt for bamboo-eating, granting more points than tile-playing, or go for growing bamboo for the difficult big points!
Also this game has a push-pull dynamic where the players play off of other players` action`s. You playing more tiles, growing bamboo, or moving panda can open up more opportunities for your opponents.
What also works for this game is the very cute and flavorful aesthetic.

RATING: 6
A cutely produced game of trying to grow bamboo in various configurations and then eating it with a panda to score points.  A silly theme, but it really makes the game!

Basically, you have a hand of goal cards which score you points.  Some will want you to make the game board tiles configure in a certain way.  Others will want specific bamboos growing on the board.  And others will want your panda to eat certain types of bamboo.  On your turn, you get a few actions in order make all of these things match your goal cards.

Once someone fulfills 8 goals, whoever has the most points worth of goals fulfilled wins!

Honestly, the game itself is probably a 5 for me, but the production quality of this game really bumps it up a notch.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.5
As my collection grows, I find myself trying harder to find those "diamonds in the rough", the good / great games (i.e. those I would rate "8" or above) that are ranked outside the Top 500.  This game is one of them.  When I first saw it in the store, I thought it was based on an anime and I was immediately prejudiced against it.  However, Bauza's name caught my eye and after watching the Cat & Mouse video on the game, I was intrigued.  The theme is quirky and cute (and certainly helped to get the girlfriend to play!).  More importantly, the tight integration of tile placement, set collection, and hidden objectives under the hood of a simple action point system makes for a fluid and engaging game from beginning to end - it also plays in less than an hour.  A top-notch, light-to-medium-weight game!

RATING: 5
I was surprised that I actually liked Takenoko as much as I did as it’s a very light game. And I doubt I would play it more than 5 times, but still, it was an enjoyable experience. Granted, I’ve only played it with 2 players, which I’m pretty sure is the most strategic player number; at least that was what I saw in my game in which I could plan quite a bit as I knew only one other played could change the situation on the board before it’s my turn again (but that can be said about most games). I would guess it’s a little more loose with 3 while 4 is probably too chaotic and hard to plan ahead.

There is a sizable amount of luck in Takenoko – it is a light family game after all. For instance, you roll a dice at the beginning of your turn, and it’s so much better to roll the ? and the extra action (almost always)… And then there are the random terrain tile draws and especially the card draws. 
The latter did actually decide my last game; I used my last action to draw a terrain objective card which I couldn’t solve. My opponent also used his last turn to draw a terrain card; a card which we could obviously both solve, but he did and got 3 points for that... I ended the game, but that meant that my opponent got an extra turn (compared to me) in which he luckily drew that card and ended up winning by 1 point! That rubbed me the wrong way. But hey, it’s not a ”gamer’s game”, it’s a light family game which has a cute theme, good components and is visually appealing, and I would definitely recommend people with kids picking it up! Also, I always love game which feature “secret objectives” so you plan your actions around some missions which only you can accomplish.

RATING: 8
I picked up Takenoko because I was hoping to find a good board game to play with my girlfriend, who's not much of a gamer. After a few plays, I found that the theme was charming, the pieces were beautiful and high-quality, and the gameplay was actually quite engaging.

What I like most about Takenoko though is that I can bring it out to play with almost any group. It's a great casual game that I can play with family members, friends, gamers, and yes, my girlfriend. :) The level of depth in the game and the different paths to score points mean that experienced gamers can have a good time, and casual players or those new to the hobby won't feel overwhelmed by dozens of minute rules. The gameplay is intuitive and fun: Get cards, expand the garden, grow bamboo, eat bamboo.

A lot of people have brought up the complaint that the victory point cards are too random and don't require any skill to fulfill, and I'll admit that this is kind of true. There's an "advanced" rule that you can use that requires you to discard and redraw VP cards if they've already been fulfilled on the board, and this does make it less random. But if you're coming to Takenoko for deep strategy and no luck, you're expecting the wrong thing. The game's level of randomness feels just right for the light theme.

Overall, a great game for mixed groups of players or new/casual players, with awesome pieces and a wonderful theme. I would highly recommend Takenoko for anyone looking for a light, carefree game or a game they can pick up and play with almost anyone.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
[b]After reading through the rules[/b] Takenoko is a conceptually very simple game in which players try to complete various simple topological and set objectives set against a bamboo garden, but are restrained by items which can be used by everyone. These items include irrigation channels (which allow bamboo to be watered), a gardener (who grows the bamboo), and a roaming panda (which eats the bamboo). Because the game uses such a mechanism, [i]and[/i] relies on a die to insert some extra randomness in what players can do every round, I expect this game to be very take that-y and tactical. And that's a shame, because I remember liking the idea of a panda roaming a bamboo garden when it was first presented for Spiel 2010 (yes, 'ten', not 'eleven'). I'm putting the game on my reserve game list for Spiel 2011: might be fun to try when there is still time left.

[b]After playing[/b] There is some strategy in how you plan your assignments, because as the garden fills up the gardening assignments become easier to fulfill. At the same time that means that someone else might already be close to finishing the game with nothing done but simple assignments. You can definitely decide how you want to play the game, that's a good thing. But with more players it's really too much about unintentional coincidences to be interesting. Too bad, the backstory is nice. That said, the game is good family material, though.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.4
It's nice to run into a game where the play lives up to the visual impact.  When you first look at Takenoko, it's hard not to be charmed by the hungry panda, the harried gardener, and those pastel bamboo pieces.

Luckily the gameplay is just as enjoyable.  Players take two actions (generally they must be different) which involve growing bamboo, moving around the pieces, or laying new tiles.  Eventually you try to complete objective cards that come in three types.  Once someone hits the magic number, the player with the most points on those cards wins.

It's quite simple, yet requires enough thinking to be a satisfying time for most gamers.  There's a bit of a puzzle element layered with some planning which should scratch the right itch.  And it's so CUTE.

RATING: 5
Great theme and "feel." Seems like a fun game the first few times, but then the obvious imbalances impose themselves. The nature of the goal cards and their point spread and ease of accomplishment are all out of whack: panda cards are personal points, no one else can get them, but tile display and bamboo grow cards can be shared- this fundamental difference causes problems. Panda cards are, for the most part, very simple to accomplish and generally you are forced, to be competitive, to do about 50% of them.

Other things are too luck based: the tile modifiers require you to roll 1/6th chance in a game where you may only get six turns. So streaky luck kills the fun. It's just too long of a game with too few of those rolls for it to work.

I don't hate it, and would play it, but I don't take it too seriously.

RATING: 7
[Unknown] - 7.5 (12 plays)
This is one of the better gateway games I've played. The theme draws in non-gamers, the rules can be explained in 10 minutes, the components are of decent quality and it plays in about an hour. The color contrasts used in this game proved successful for the color blind player in our group. For gamers looking for more meat, it still has luck built into the game - tile draw, card draw and the weather die. Some of it can be mitigated, but some is just luck. Given how much of a hit it is with non-gamers, this will remain in the collection.

[16 Jan 2018] - 7 (12 plays)
Dropping the rating to a 7. The game does have a fatal flaw in the rules that makes it too easy to run up a huge score without going through the rest of the game. Knowing this flaw, it's easier to play the metagame and the whole experience isn't any fun. I still think this is a great game to keep and pull out when trying to play a game with non-gamers. The panda figure, light rules and colorful artwork appeals to that crowd.

RATING: 7
Players are gardeners the royal garden of the emperor of Japan, tending the bamboo plants and keeping the hungry panda (a gift from China) happy.  Super cute game, where players take turns choosing two actions from a list of five possibilities.  Actions include expanding the garden (hex tiles), moving the gardener (causing bamboo to grow), moving the panda (who eats bamboo!), irrigating the garden, or choosing a hidden victory point goal.  Bamboo comes in three colours - pink, yellow and green.  The object is to complete the secret objective cards, to earn victory points.  The cards award points for matching the garden layout, growing bamboo in certain combinations of colour and height, or feeding the panda certain bamboo colour combinations.  A very easy game to teach and play, and it reminds me a lot of hidden objective games such as Ticket to Ride and Ankh-Morpork.  The looks absolutely beautiful on the table too - the stackable wooden bamboo pieces are stunning, and the rest of the game isn't too shabby either.  Well worth a look.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Idea:
Grow bamboo and feed panda with it.

Mechanism:
get two actions + one die rolled action per round. Board will consist of three different colors that grow its color of bamboo
Create board while you play and try to fill out goal cards that either require certain formation of board tiles on play or certain bamboo growth on board or fed certain types of bamboo to panda.

Quite easy to learn and still has some replayability. Good for kids.

Special: Played big version of game where tiles and tokes were way bigger than normal like 15cm. Very cute layout.

RATING: 9
Nagyszerű családi játék. Egyszerű és logikus szabályok, ami először egy kezdőnek soknak tűnhet. Ezért nem "getaway" játék. Egyébként tökéletesen összerakott, egyedi hangulattal rendelkező kis játék, aminek minden eleme a helyén van és jól használható. Csak ajánlani tudom! (2014.03.22.)
3 játék után kicsit egyenlőtlennek érzem a célkártyákat, ami nem von le a játék élményfaktorából szerencsére. Még nem néztem utána a fórum oldalakon, de az eddigi játékok alapján mintha a parcella célkártyákat aránytalanul nehéz lenne teljesíteni, az értük járó díjazást tekintve. Ezzel szemben nálunk a kertész kártyák voltak a legnépszerűbbek. Mindenesetre a játékélmény továbbra is kiváló, megérte beszerezni a játékot! (2014.03.24.)
Kipróbáltam egy másik stratégiát, s arra jöttem rá, ha 3 fős játéknál ketten is a pandás célkártyára gyúrnak, annak esélye sincs, aki a kertész célkártyákkal próbálkozik. A lényeg, hogy érdemes a többiek játékát figyelni, s ahhoz igazítani a sajátunkat. Még mindig kiváló családi játéknak tartom, ahol azért kell egy tanuló játék, amíg a szabályok tisztázódnak, de utána felhőtlen a szórakozás :). (2014.03.26.)
Új játékosoknak rendszeresen meggyűlik a bajuk egy-egy szabály értelmezésével, de a második játékra általában kikristályosodik a kép. Mostanában a panda célkártya lett a menő, az fogy el a játék végére. A parcellás célkártyák pedig szerintem a játék egyetlen hibája (ha a szerencse faktort elfogadjuk). A hangulata továbbra is kiváló és egyik menet sem ugyanolyan, így az újrajátszhatósági faktora is rendkívül magas. Megunhatatlan - egyenlőre. (2014.03.28.)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This game is a little deceptive.  After new gamers get past the usual set of gateway games (your Ticket to Rides, your Carcassone’s, your Alhambra’s, your basic Dominion sets), I pull this little game out.  They look at the cute little panda and the little pastel bamboo stalks, roll their eyes and say, ‘you’ve got to be kidding?!?’  But after a few rounds (of not really taking it seriously), a realization starts to dawn on them that this cute little game actually packs a punch.  They suddenly realize they’ve got to start to plan sequences of events in advance and look at the game board as a real puzzle to solve.  That smirk on their face turns into a stare of deep concentration as the board expands and the puzzle in front of them becomes more complex and something of a challenge.  They hold their breath as another player moves the gardener or the panda and reconfigures the bamboos, possibly to their detriment.   
However, to make this game a bit more balanced and more of a challenge, I would recommend playing the game with your objective cards open on the table so that other players can see how their actions could potentially reward or block other players.  However, if the group is prone to Analysis Paralysis, you might want to forget about that option.  Additionally, the optional rule (mentioned in the rulebook) of only allowing new objectives to be taken by players that haven’t already been achieved, is both good and fair.  
It would be great if the designers could find a way to come out with an expansion to add a 5th player.

RATING: N/A
It's a light and fun game to play, but I don't feel I need to own this.

I certainly admire the objective card mechanic in the game. You get points by following what your objective card shows. Throughout the game, you can draw more objective cards to score more points. Basically, this is what runs the game.

Great pieces but the copy I played (own by a boardgame cafe) was heavily worn out (the cardboard pieces), obviously due to bad handling by players. 

From the designer of 7 Wonders, what a surprise!

I think it is an OK game to me. Nothing great or nothing spectacular. Still, like I said, I admire the in-game objective cards.

RATING: 6
Rating lowered.  As one of my earlier purchases, I was predisposed to liking Takenoko.  What's not to like?  It's colorful, has a simple ruleset and it's lovingly produced (I have the larger 1st-edition).  It always draws a crowd because it just looks so good, but as they say, looks aren't everything.

It's hard to recommend Takenoko as a family game or a gateway game.  There's simply not enough meat on its bones to hook a noob into the hobby and as far as family games go, so long as you only want to play it the one time, it'll be fine.  In the end, I feel like there's just a fun-factor that's missing.  It doesn't make it a bad game, mind you, and I'll gladly sit down to play it because it does its job as a nice, short, low-complexity game.  But the luck-based nature of its mechanics combined means you're really just going through the motions and you're never really quite engaged.  On both categories of family and gateway, there are better choices out there.

If anything, Takenoko is like a walk through a park on a sunny day at the perfect temperature - it's an enjoyable experience, but I'd still rather be doing something else.

RATING: 7.75
This is a light weight action-selection game about the interactions between a gardener and panda in the imperial garden of the Japanese emperor.  Players choose actions such as laying down a plot of land, irrigating a field, using the gardener to grow bamboo, or moving the panda to eat the bamboo.  Players score points based on goal cards that require either certain types of bamboo to be consumed, a certain level of bamboo growth, or a certain pattern of irrigated fields.

The game is really easy to learn and pretty fun to play.  It contains a good dose of luck in the form of the goal cards drawn and a die roll to determine a bonus action.  The game is also really aesthetically pleasing with its bright colors and 3D element when the bamboo start growing.  This is a great family or gateway game to introduce people into the hobby.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 5
The most appealing part of this game is the components. They are colourful, appealing and of high quality. They will draw almost anyone to your table to investigate and can be an incentive for new players. I enjoyed the shifting weather patterns and the variety of point-scoring options.

We struggled a bit with formulating strategies early on. As the game played, we found that an opponent was just as likely to complete one of our objectives as we were. There was a feeling that as players we had little control over our success.

Takenoko feels chaotic and left us a little unsatisfied, but it's a very cute chaotic and it can still be fun.

-------------Original rating 17/10/15 Score:7
[b]Rating based on - 100+ plays, 2 player - 3 player - 4 player
Preferred player Count: 2 or 3[/b]
I learned and played this game online at Board Game Arena. It took me a few plays to 'get' the game, but once I did it ended up being really fun and slightly addictive. I now kick azz at it :) I feel the cards could use a better balance - 1 bamboo grown 4 high on a fertiliser tile is easy enough to complete relatively painlessly (can even be done in the same turn!), but 4 green bamboo 3 high is super difficult and I always seem to draw that one...aaargh! Aside from that, I love the way the game plays, I love the artwork, and I love the components. If a good deal fell into my lap I'd consider it, but I'm not actively seeking out a copy. A few things keep me from  pulling the trigger on this one:
Do I need another light/family weight/tile placement/set collecting game? My collection has ample amounts of all.
How is game maintenance/upkeep in real life? Seems like it would be kind of tedious and fiddly with placing which bamboo segments grow, removing bamboo, growing only where irrigated etc.
[b]Status: KEEPER[/b]

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
A "mission completion", family game where you're trying to complete different missions on three types of cards. You're either getting colored tiles in certain configurations, growing bamboo stalks to certain heights, or having the panda eat certain colored bamboo stalks. You get two actions per turn and start your turn rolling the die for a special bonus which may be an extra action that turn or something else that assists you towards your missions. 

Due to the die roll which may offer you exactly what you need or be useless and the randomness of other people unknowingly stepping on your plans (e.g., having the panda eat the bamboo you were trying to grow), there's a good bit of luck here in how many times your little spider has to go back up the water spout. 

The production is excellent and the game exudes a high cuteness factor. The panda and farmer figures that come with the game are painted plastic minis not meeples (pandeeple?) and the bamboo stalks look great as they populate the board. A great family offering but not enough substance here for more serious gamers.

RATING: 6.5
Takenoko is a beautiful, light game involving tile placement making up a shared board, stacking wooden pieces (growing bamboo) and moving a panda and a gardener in straight lines across the board in order to meet objectives specific to me.  It's not a heavy game, but it may take non-gamers a bit of time to get used to the idea of sharing all components but the cards.  I'm not usually a fan of hidden objectives in games, and that's the whole game in this case.  But it's pretty and simple enough that I won't mind it bringing it out occasionally, and I know my girls will absolutely love it.

RATING: 6.5
Helyes kis játék, amit valószínőleg szinte bárki szívesen játszik. Szabályai arányleg egyszerűek, de azért a kezdőknek lehetnek vele problémái. A kivitelézés gyönyörű.

A játék folyamán területlapkákat kell letennünk, azokon bambuszt növesztenünk víz és kertészünk segítségével, illetve bambuszt leenni a pandával. A pontokat háromféle titkos célkártya adja, amikből a játék folyamán szerezhetünk még.

Mivel a célkártyákat és területlapokat is véletlenszerűen húzzuk így szerencse szerepe szerintem igen a nagy játékban. Ezen felül érzésem szerint csak evésre van értelme mennünk, mivel azzal szinte biztosan nem segítünk senkinek (jó esélllyel inkább hátráltatjuk a többieket), míg magunkanak gyűlnek a pontok. A másik két céllaptípust jóval nehezebb teljesíteni, ráadásul közben másnak is kikaparhatod a gesztenyét. Ugyan ezek több pontot hoznak a konyhára, de szerintem nem eléggé.

Kedves ki színes családi játék, amiben kicsit lehet agyalni is, de ne várjon senki mondjuk tikal szintű játékmenetet.

RATING: 5
Takenoko is pretty good family entertainment, but exactly how much of that is due to presentation is debatable. The game looks gorgeous, there's no denying that. The way the goal cards are assigned and completed, however, inserts a lot of randomness into an already chaotic game. Some people will get their goals served on a silver platter, others will have their carefully groomed bamboo garden inadvertently trampled on by the other players. The game is pretty quick so that is not the end of the world but if a game's primary selling point is good looks, that is rarely a compliment.

RATING: 7.7
Fun game, although the strategy is a little light. My main complaint is the cards. There are 3 categories of cards, each with their own merit in terms of difficulty. What I don't like is that the point values for each card seem arbitrary. Many cards that clearly require more energy to fulfill are worth 2 or 3 points, while some Panda cards that take almost no effort to fulfill are worth 5 or 6 points. If the points were distributed based on difficulty of completing the card then I think this could be a great game. As it is, it's just a fun cute game.

RATING: N/A
{"sleeves":[{"44x68":46,"sleeved":true}]}
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Un ami, plutôt axé jeux sans trop de hasard et relativement calculatoires, a une compagne. Celle-ci est assez joueuse, tant par sa volonté propre que sous les harcèlements de cet ami. Mais le souci, c'est que leurs goûts se rejoignent parfois, mais qu'en général il y a une rupture visuelle. Alors devant un petit panda et un style assez "kawaï", elle a craqué. Et lui, dans une démarche de compromis bien évidente, accepte de jouer à "Takenoko", bien que ce ne soit pas son type de jeu favori (un peu trop light). Et c'est comme ça que je me suis retrouvé à y jouer.

Depuis, on débat souvent sur la qualité et l'intérêt de celui-ci. Sachant que lui y a beaucoup plus joué que moi, il en est un peu lassé et ne le sort pas vraiment avec plaisir. Pour ma part, je trouve ce format plus léger et familial/rapide est vraiment agréable, tant qu'on ne s'attend pas à un jeu avec des mécanismes compliqués ou avec un profondeur inouïe. Mais nous débattons aussi régulièrement sur la difficulté attribuée à un jeu. Car moi, ma chérie, n'est pas joueuse du tout. Sauf quelques jeux d'ambiance, mais ça s'arrête là. Et même un jeu comme "Takenoko", c'est trop. Du coup ça me donne une autre vision des choses. Ce jeu est certes familial, mais pour des personnes désirant s'investir dans le monde ludique, pas pour des gens qui repoussent le monde du jeu de société. Dès qu'il y a quelques subtilités (et il y en a dans "Takenoko"), plus de trois paragraphes de règles, ça peut repousser et être vécu comme sortant du pur divertissement. Ce qu'on trouve tous les deux dommage, bien sûr, mais bon, respectons les choix de chacun.

Donc voilà, on a une approche un peu différente de cet objet ludique. Lui en a ras-le-bol du hasard mis en place par le dé et le tirage aléatoire des objectifs, qui peut bloquer et laisser un joueur à la traîne sans qu'il n'ait l'impression de mal jouer ou de faire les mauvais choix. Pour ma part, ce genre de paramètres ne me gêne que peu dans ce format de jeu et j'apprécie qu'il y ait une forme de hasard dans le jeu, auquel on doit s'adapter. Et je ne dis pas ça parce que je fais des jets de malade, la dernière fois c'est moi qui en ai souffert d'ailleurs, mais ça ne m'a pas gêné. Car si le jeu est vraiment simple au niveau des choix à faire, il bénéficie de mécanismes très fluides et rend l'ensemble efficace. Pour moi, "Takenoko" est donc un très bon jeu dans ce format, qui peut servir à initier des nouveaux joueurs qui acceptent d'écouter des règles plus d'1m30. Je prends un plaisir à y jouer, c'est souvent des parties assez tranquilles, même si ce n'est pas l'extase ludique et que ce format n'est sans doute pas mon favori, il est nécessaire et agréable et l'As d'or le valorise d'une belle manière en récompensant "Takenoko".

Au moins, nous sommes entièrement d'accord sur un point. Le visuel et la qualité du matériel. C'est assez constant chez Matagot, d'une part ça attire l’œil en magasin et permet de faire découvrir le monde du jeu à de nouveaux clients, d'autre part ça donne vraiment envie d'y jouer, quelque soit le joueur. Les couleurs sont plaisantes, et le fait de voir les bambous grandir est quelque chose que j'apprécie beaucoup. Le thème est donc très bien adapté, pas spécialement aux mécanismes, mais à l'esprit et au sentiment général du jeu. Ce qui est l'une des grandes forces d'Antoine Bauza.

RATING: 6.5
I should like this base game more but the scoring system from mission-card-only is poor.
1) Very hard to catch up the leader in each game
2) Drawing troll who intend to draw a lot of tiles or gardener mission card can win too easy in 4 players game.
3) Panda mission is easy but it require your 2-3 actions to complete each one while score of each card is too low. The more your try to finish Panda card, the more chance you lost game.

I like this game more when I bought the Chibi expansion. It add baby pandas point that you can convert an action into points plus benefit from baby panda. Sometime it help us to catch up with the leader in game. Situation can be flipped anytime if you're solely focusing on mission point. It add more fun back to game.
So if you like this game. I'd recommend to add Chibi expansion as well.

RATING: 6
I've been waiting a long time to finally play Takenoko. First off, it's a cute game! It has a pleasant feel to how one plays their turn. At the end of the day though, I feel luck and randomness really play too much of a role here.  I found the whether die could really influence what a player could do- either give a huge bonus or stick you with some useless crap. The point system on the cards didn't seem balanced; even though there are less of some colours (so more points are awarded for them) our board was very asymmetrical to how it should have looked given the tile distribution. Perhaps tile manipulation is too easy here? Anyway, I also found by the end it was a 40-50% chance that you could draw a score card where the requirements were already fulfilled or at least one step away. Made for boring game play. Fortunately, I don't think Takenoko tries to be anything more than what it is, so I don't fault it for being too light for my tastes. I'm sure this is a great game to get kids into some of the more subtler flavours of modern board games.

RATING: 8.5
This is one beautiful game that not only looks great, but is lots of fun to play. The game is easy to teach/learn and plays fairly quick. It makes for a wonderful family game, that even gamers may enjoy. I know I do.

There is some luck involved, with the draw of the cards, but nothing to severe. I really like how fast the turns go, so as to not have a lot of down time in between players.

I'd highly recommend that everyone at least try this game.

RATING: 6.5
Beautiful components and the game really is quick to teach and play. It seems like its hard to find fault but I do have some slight qualms...it's nearly impossible to willingly ruin your opponents plans because there are simply too many random objective cards and too few actions per turn. You're virtually guaranteed to use all of your actions with the sole intent on satisfying only your personal objectives. (Granted, you can screw up your opponents plans on accident trying to fulfill your own.)
One of the bigger complaints is that some of the objective cards seem way more valuable and easy to complete than others. The panda eating 2 reds for 5 points for example. Im not sure know why I would ever take a card for tile pattern objectives when I could get the easy and valuable panda food cards. The gardner cards also because they are worth more.
Its a good game, but a little too much luck involved.

RATING: 4
I think of this game as convoluted and worse Ticket to Ride. Just like in TtR, you draw some goals and hope to fulfil them and all of the interaction is hoping that no one else takes your spot. The difference here is that the goals are more random so there's no way to know if you're helping or hurting your opponents. This makes the game very random and every turn feels somewhat pointless. The rules are also needlessly complicated, which makes it unappealing for many TtR fans.

RATING: 7
My husband and I give Takenoko a rating of 7 with two players. We haven't played with more people yet. The rules are clearly written and simple to grasp, and we can remember all of them without frequent references to the rulebook. The variety of actions provide plenty of scope for exploring different strategies, yet the limited number of actions to take each turn keep us from feeling overwhelmed by choices. The theme is peaceful and supports the game mechanisms well. The components are well-made and look pretty on the table. Luck is a definite element, but not so strong that it overwhelms skill. We think that Takenoko will become a perennial favorite.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Looks like a game of an asian designer but no, he is French. The theme and grafic style aims at families and the designer succeeded in creating a game that is not difficult to understand but still offers many ways to go for victory. This was a surprise as I initially thought this game would fail with me. Good written rules too. Rating after one game (7).

edit: I really enjoyed my first game but after my second game I had to downrate it. The game lacks of depth and interaction.
An "advanced" rule says: "If a player picks an objective card already completed in the bamboo garden, he must discard it and picks a new objective card". I the later game I choose an plot card and yep I had to discard it, as it was already fulfilled. So as the next and the next and the ubernext. I just emptied half of the objective pile. Then I changed to gardener objectifs and even there the first two cards were already fulfilled. I really consider it as a design flaw if you are somehow urged to throw away 10+ cards until you get a "valid" one.

RATING: 7
A pleasing game about a gardener and a panda that won't stop eating his bamboo. Every turn the player rolls the Weather dice and does two actions, which usually can't be repeated. They're mostly about placing new tiles,  irrigating terrain and moving the characters to grow bamboo (gardener) and eat it (panda). The main goal is to complete success conditions on goal cards.

RATING: 1
Like Ticket To Ride -- too slow for a gateway game, and success is based on whether you draw the right objective cards late in the game when it's possible to achieve them trivially.

And the cuteness stops mattering quickly because the game is pretty abstract. If only Bauza designed games that feel special, in addition to looking special.

Redeeming factor: Having a different number of tiles in each color adds interesting texture.

RATING: 6
On the good side, the competition in the game can get exciting towards the end.  The board space and components draw non-players in to see what's going on.  And the art and component quality are very high.

On the not so good side, there are a couple of broken parts --- for example, the weather die can often, especially in late game, affect no one in any way. Also, like Tokaido, while it's a beautifully done theme, it's not terribly intriguing.

On the whole it's a solid game with interesting (though not truly thrilling) choices. I imagine it'd be a good intro game, and would work especially well with the 8-12 yr old crowd.

RATING: 5.5
It may work as a family game, despite the excess of randomness and lack of balance. It's common to draw objective cards that have been already completed and score easy points (or almost completed, if you use the optional rule of discarding completed ones). Interaction between players is limited to unknowingly helping your opponents complete objectives or messing with them a bit. But the is mildly pleasant and relaxing. The excellent production, with beautiful artwork, cool "bamboo" pieces and painted miniatures, surely helps a lot in its success.

RATING: 7.5
2-4 Players
Best 3
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This game's theme is superb! It could not be about anything other than a panda eating away at your garden's bamboo. All the mechanics fit in really well.

The game's art/design is very well executed too. There's the rulebook (which includes a lovely comic), the beautiful box (all components fit snugly and it stays on the table as bamboo reserve), the great drawings all over and of course the ingenious bamboo.

It all makes for a very accessible and fun game.

A possible downside of the game: 
The luck of the draw is very decisive. Different values are attached to each colour (pink=highest, green=lowest) and I don't think these differences are leveled out by a supposed difficulty level of completing each objective.

RATING: 10
My favorite game EVER. It's so cute and colorful and has a PANDA. But don't be fooled! There is a lot going on here and there can be a lot of strategy involved. Weather patterns are a nice element. They add a tiny bit of chance to the game without it being ruled by random dice rolls. The weather patterns really only effect optional things you can do on your turn like eat a piece of bamboo anywhere, grow one piece of bamboo anywhere, pick up a helpful token, take a 3rd action or ability to repeat 2 of the same actions on your turn. They can help and add some bit of spontaneity, but they don't wreck your strategy either.

5-28-15
An interesting game in that you can approach winning in three different ways.  Finding a blend of the three works best, yet two of the goals (panda vs. gardener) will generally act against one another.  You can see which cards others have though, and try to balance your objectives accordingly.

I feel like the tile placement objectives may be too easily reached, especially in the late game.  Maybe better panda/gardener play would help eliminate that risk.

RATING: 7
Nagyon kellemes hangulatú családi játék. Hatalmas szerencsefaktor van benne, mert a célkártyákat véletlenszerűen húzzuk fel. És ha olyat kapunk a kertészből amin külön jelölő kell és nem dobunk a kockával olyat, amelyből ilyen jelölőt felvehetünk, máris ez a kártya feleslegesen foglalja a kezünkben a helyet. Más meg felhúz olyan kártyát, amely rögtön meg is valósult már és azonnal írja a pontot. A gyakorlottabb játékosok nem is rakják ki az összes elkészült lapjaikat, hanem amikor már a vége felé van a játéknak, egyszerre játsszák ki őket.

Több mint 40 játékkal a hátam mögött, egyértelműen kijelenthető, hogy nagyon nagy a szerencse szerepe a játékban, egyrészt a kockadobás másrészt a kártyahúzás miatt. Semmiféle mechanizmus nincs a játékban a rossz dobások és a rossz laphúzások ellensúlyozására.  
Ezért az eredeti 8-as osztályzatot 7-esre módosítom.

We really love this game. It is imbalanced, so you'll probably have to house rule things to make it a better play. A good rule that I've heard is that you only get points for cards you complete if you've complete them in a set (one of each kind). Another recommended one is that you discard a card if you can immediately complete it when you draw it. 

Regardless, it's a light game with enough decisions to keep people entertained and invested. Plus, there's a Panda!

RATING: 5
I have to admit that when my friend asked me to look at the box to Takenoko and asked me what I thought, I summarily dismissed it out of hand based on the pink bamboo and cartoon panda.  Boy, was that foolish of me!  This is a very fun light strategy game.  Purists will deride the excessive element of luck via the weather die rolled before each turn as well as drawing objective cards--which range from being able to complete with one simple action to an epic project like digging the Panama Canal.  However, if you can accept the element of luck, the game is very entertaining, it is relatively simple and easy to share with non-gamers, and plays in a relatively short amount of time.

RATING: 9
This is my new favorite game. I've played several times and it never gets old. This is a great game for us women. 

There's no violence, nor offensive graphics, nor sexist language (other than the directions assuming all players are men.) This is probably the most feminist game I've played in several years, in that it doesn't gender the game other than one set of bamboo (out of 3) is pink.

My hubby and son love this game as much as I do, as do some of the men in our gamer groups.

This is a game tweens & teens would love. It plays best with 3-4 players.

RATING: 7
Saw this game in my local game store, with the charming art design and concept piquing my curiosity. After reading some mixed reviews, I decided to take a chance on it...

What I found was a simple, but beautiful and elegant game. The theme and components (as everyone seems to mention) really shine, and the game is almost meditative to play. It's pretty straightforward, with juuuust enough player interaction (or interference, one could say) to make things interesting without infringing upon the peaceful spirit of the game. Quite a lovely experience. 

I personally found that the tile cards didn't reward nearly enough points for the amount of work they usually require, so when I play I just double their point values. It has made for a much more balanced game, in my experience.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Takenoko is one of the most visually appealing games I've seen. The artwork is on point and the components, including a pair of nice, painted miniatures, is top-notch.

The game isn't too bad either - it has the makings of a simple abstract game that hides it depth. It does seem a bit unbalanced, however, as feeding the Panda seems to be the easiest way to victory (either that or having other players accidentally accomplish one's objectives).

My other main complaint is that the rules are a bit clunky. It is very easy to overlook a rule. Still, it's a nice production and a pleasant game that I enjoy from time-to-time.

RATING: 8.3
Cute and fun, Takenoko is a relaxing game of completing requests of the emperor. The quests fall into 3 basic catagories; Feed the panda, organize the gardens, and grow bamboo in a specific way. The twist is, if someone else completes your request for you, you can cash in on their hard work. Or if you suspect someone is trying to complete a specific request, you can throw a monkey wrench into their plans.

It's a pretty chill game, great for families. Its great with all player counts (2-4) The competitive elements are very light. Fantastic icebreaker game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Collector's edition takes up quite a bit of space on the table but looks great once you're into it. Simple rules but quite enjoyable.

Gardener is trying to tend his garden and grow bamboo while the panda runs around eating the bamboo. Try to gain the emperors favor by trimming down bamboo or laying out tiles in specific patterns.

Just watch out for the collectors edition weather dice, it's a little unwieldly and could possibly do some damage due to it's size, highly recommend using a dice try to roll it or any other soft surface.

RATING: 5.5
2013-04-15

Initial Rating: 5.5 (April 2013)

I was pleasantly surprised by the game. A lot of gamer friends said to me that I would not like Takenoko, so I was expecting a bad game but it wasn’t the case. The game is gorgeous and pretty simple. It can be taught under 10 minutes. The game components are also very good.

The gameplay is pretty decent, however I’m a little worried about the game balance due to the cards. I feel they add a lot of luck to the game. Still as it is a light (and quick) gateway game I don´t care much. However I’m rating Takenoko a 5.5 due to the luck of the draw in the cards.

Bottom line, Takenoko is a game I would play again but not one I would like to own (although my girlfriend loves it). Perfect for families or to introduce new people to our beloved hobby :).

Current Rating: 5.5

RATING: 7
Attractively produced lightweight Euro, with fun gameplay. After a game or two I'd recommend the variant that prevents the re-scoring of cards (tile combos in particular, the gardener and panda cards are ok) that have already been scored, as otherwise it can be too much of a luck-fest with players just drawing score cards (especially the tile cards) in the late game hoping to re-score tile combos in play that have already been scored.

RATING: 8
This is one of our go-to favorites. It's simple enough to be played when you don't feel like thinking hard, complex enough to keep it interesting, and cute enough to keep you squealing. It's a game where you are completing secret goals and building a world one tile at a time with other people who also have secret goals. Goals include either building a certain color tile combination, eating a certain color bamboo combination, or growing a certain color bamboo combination. It's very fun and the expansion added a lot of really interesting game tiles to the mix. Great game.

RATING: 4
Oh Takenoko how much I want to love you... but alas it cannot be. I will start out by saying that the game is absolutely gorgeous. The components are of the best quality and the game looks great on the table once you are done playing it. The main problem I have is that it is absolutely and completely random to the point where I feel as if there is not point in playing it because the winner is arbitrary anyways. You can pick up a card that is almost complete and score 6 points or you can spend 4 turns working on a card that is worth 3 points. Still, I know that this game has a following as it is so highly rated and at least it is done quickly so that's a plus right? Buyer beware!

RATING: 6
Very good game. Even for introducing new people.

I should have rated it a 7... but there can be a lot of take-that that just... doesn't feel in the spirit of the game?

So your objective is depending on your cards. Cultivate certain bamboo strains in your garden in a certain configuration. Have the panda eat a certain mix of bamboo. Or have bamboo sprouts form a pleasing configuration...
You do this by performing two different actions each turn, with a die added to mix this up a bit.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
In this game you're building a garden and growing bamboo but also feeding a panda who eats the bamboo.  You each have different cards with VP conditions so you're trying to manipulate the garden to satisfy those conditions to score VP.  When a player has scored 7 cards the game ends and the other players will have one chance to beat the score.

Szerintem alap, hogy a már teljesített kártyát visszarakjuk és újat húzunk helyette, illetve a játék végén jár a +3 pont a 3 különböző cél teljesítéséért. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Given to my daughter, who really enjoys it. :)

This little panda has won a special place at my gaming table. This gorgeous little game has beautiful components (though the cards are a little flimsy, you just use them for scoring), a clear, entertaining and educational rulebook, and plenty of fun and fast-paced gameplay. I play this as a family game, and it is quite competitive! The cooperative building of the map you all share, plus your mutual manipulation of the panda and gardener make it interactive without being cut-throat. I do have two complaints, though. Since the cards vary so much in value, bad draws can easily cost you the game. And because these cards are kept secret, it's impossible to interfere with another player's strategy. This makes it much better suited as a family game than it is a strategy game.

RATING: 9
I wanted to give this a 10. There is SO MUCH going right with this game: depth of strategy, neat theme, quick play.

The one reason I cannot rate this 10 for 10 are the relative variance in how the game can play out too quickly for one player if they push some tile laying strategies and get the right tile VP cards.  I think this strategy is easily mitigated with savvy players, but the rush strategy can be a little warping.

I like the amount of normal variance in the game, and I love the end game visual appeal, much like carcassonne, it's a beautiful game to play and to finish.

RATING: 7
I got this game for my birthday in 2016. I really liked the pictures and videos of it, that I had seen on the web. The artwork is just beautiful. I was hoping for this to be a great family game to play with my relatives and with children, but after introducing it to a few people, it turned out it was actually slightly hard to grasp for some of them. Too light for my gamer friends. but too heavy for many non gamers I know. So unfortunately it doesn't see as much play as I had hoped for. I guess it will be a "next step game" for some non gamers I play with.

RATING: N/A
In Takenoko, the players will cultivate land plots, irrigate them, and grow one of the three species of bamboo (Green, Yellow and Pink) with the help of the Imperial gardener to maintain this bamboo garden. They will have to bear with the immoderate hunger of this sacred animal for the juicy and tender bamboo. The player who manages his land plots best, growing the most bamboo while feeding the delicate appetite of the panda, will win the game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
► Best family game.

[b]Takenoko[/b] works wonderfully as a family game: cute theme, fantastic components, easy rules, great iconography (making it language-independent), it's shining with colour and has a very low level of competition.

It arguably also works as a next step beyond the usual gateway games for newcomers to the hobby -- and my rating is based on exactly these aspects.

For seasoned board game fans, [b]Takenoko[/b] can still be a nice relaxing experience from time to time, because of the mentioned qualities this game has, but it can also completely fall flat if players are looking for a game with real depth.

The main reason [b]Takenoko[/b] plays like a nice low-competitive game is, that the objective cards from other players are hidden, which means that players will only take their turns for themselves without actually knowing if they are helping their opponents.

This adds a not to underestimate level of luck to the game, and surprisingly often the person I explained this game to actually won without really knowing what they were doing.

Still, I'm rating this game for what it is and wants to be: a nice and cute family game.

Panda for President ! [microbadge=26928]

RATING: 4
The presentation is very nice and the theme is well supported. Other than that I'm not at all sure what the appeal stem from. The gameplay is very shallow, where opportunities primarily come from your opponents by accident.

I can see it work in a more social group where gameplay is secondary as there's lots of room for idle chatter, but it's 'functional' at best.

There's a tad too many minor rule details (also of the kind where, in the rules, you have to search for among the examples - which I loathe). While the rules are mostly logical with regards to theme, it's not at all intuitive. Which is a remarkable combo, really.

Oh, and it's a no-no for the colourblind amongst us.

RATING: 6.5
Very light boardgames with nice bright board and bits.  The goal card are not valued particularly well and there's a ton of randomness in getting the right ones.  The dice certainly adds even more randomness.  In the game I played, the winner won by pulling 2 random goals which happened to be already completed (board layout) worth 8 pts (on a final score of 36) in the final round.  Still, it's fast and it flows well enough that it's pleasant to play, just don't have any expectation of skill determining outcome.

RATING: 6
Panda figure & pastel colored bamboo - so I had to have it! A family game, but can also be played strategicly with gamers. You plant the royal gardens with bamboo, the gardener tends to the bamboo and the panda eats it. The game is to find patterns in the garden that corresponds to your secret missions (drawn face down). When you mission it completed you show your card and score point. Number of missions depend upon the number of players. 

Edit: There's a problem with the scoring system if you ask me. I will try to fix it and get back.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A good light game with a great theme and art. The action choices and the weather meld really well with the theme, and this game manages to combine a bunch of mechanics in small quantities (action point allowance, set collection, grid movement, etc.) without any of them feeling tacked on or clunky. 

In regards to the goal cards: metagaming the goal cards I think features too prominently in this game, and I wish there were more variety of goals in general. Also, the non-Panda goal cards outside your first batch are really luck-based, as someone might be able to score a large amount of points with little effort if the board is in their favor, while someone else might obtain one that is near impossible to achieve. However, one thing I liked of how the goals they were implemented was the maximum hand size so you can't just hoard a ton of goal cards and wait till the last half of the game to complete all of them.

RATING: 7
Takenoko is a simple set collection game where you are trying to make various sets.  You are either trying to get certain garden tiles irrigated, bamboo to grow in particular configuration or have your panda each certain kinds of bamboo.  On your turn you have two actions and a bonus action that is determined randomly with a dice roll.  

This is a very cute game.  It is possibly more luck based, but it is intended for younger kids but it is great for gamers too.  I love the game and play it with the family a good bit. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Nel proprio turno è possibile coltivare i terreni, far crescere il bambù, farlo mangiare al panda ed altre azioni.
Le carte obiettivo si completano formando una determinata composizione di terreni dei diversi colori, raggiungendo determinate altezze delle piante di bambù o di pezzi mangiati dal panda.

RATING: 8
Beautiful looking, fast, quite light game. The game is about filling different Objectives and each turn you have 2 or 3 actions depending on the Event die result. Luck seems to have a little too big impact in the form of Objective cards as their difficulty vary depending on the board state and what Objectives other players are trying to achieve. Skilled players can try to mitigate bad luck though. Each turn is a fun little puzzle until your luck turns against you and you can't really do anything.

RATING: 5
I don't really like this game. The gameplay, to me, seems to hang together by a thread. A thread so fragile that any serious experience of playing other games will break, and the game will just seem like a dislocated pile of game mechanics and actions. But ....

... my kids (the two younger ones) absolutely love it! They take great glee in moving the panda and eating my bamboo. They take great glee in being able to choose which one of the extra actions they perform after a dice role. They just enjoy every bit of it. I play it for them. For me it just doesn't sit as a comprehensive game. But I admit it does look very nice on the table.

I haven't tried playing with the variation rules whereby you get 3 points for every set of completed task cards you have (1 tile pattern, 1 bamboo collection and 1 pattern of growing bamboo). This may change it up and improve it as you are forced to go for a variety of cards during the game and not just the tile patterns which seem far easier to match and collect.

I also don't like the fact that often many cards are already or almost complete when you draw them. I do like playing you just discard these but the kids don't. Also the English rule book mentions when taking the tile action you draw three tiles and choose one and place the other two back on the top. This slows down the tile draw and on rare occasions the whole game as no-one gets what they want. We switched to playing you put them back on the bottom of the pile so you get through the tiles quicker.

I am sorry to say this is not one for me. I will trade it as soon as the kids show no interest in playing it!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Enjoyed it. Multiple plays reveal that some strategies are better than others, but with enough game sense you can take advantage of your opponents when they all try to go for i.e. the gardener objectives. There's also quite a bit of luck involved, since you have to roll the weather die, which has a 33,33% chance of being what you want, about the same chance for the land plots to be what you want and finally getting that right objective card. So 3 out of 6 actions are almost wholly reliant on luck, which might be too much for some, but it's actually nice to have luck in games to even the playground between strategic hobbyists and casual players. If Takenoko had no luck element to it, you could say it's basically a retheme of something like Splendor. But I'm glad it's not.

Would love to play this with those strategic-minded hobbyists and see if it's worthy of more stars.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Easy to learn and quick to play, with super-cute theme. Women will love it, as will men with a taste for peaceful, non-confrontational and relaxed game environment.

You pick cards from three categories of goals (shaping the garden, growing bamboos, eating bamboos) and try to do the right combos to score the points.

The panda and the gardener are moved collectively in a competition to have them do what each player needs in order to complete the goals.

If it lasted longer it would probably become a bit boring, but for a fast match it's just got what it takes to be fun. It's all about balancing your chances, maybe there's too much luck related to the die regulating the weather conditions, but not enough to spoil meaningful play.

Each player kind of plays independently, because one hardly gets enough information about the competitors' aims to make it reasonable to waste your moves to impede them. Nevertheless, the cunning player will choose moves that shrink the tree of possibilities for the following players whenever there's an opportunity to do so.


UPDATE:

I've been playing this game for years and it's still interesting. When we are two players and we don't have much time, it's almost always our first choice. I'm raising my rating because I like it even more now and I feel I underestimated its depth.

The fact that you can pick the category of your next goals and even choose which goals you want to pursue or ignore allows for a lot of more planning than I initially realised. Different goals have a different value in victory points and you can cleverly combine them to reach them faster or lower your risks. For example, if you know that you are likely to need eating some bamboo segments to shape the garden in the way prescribed by a high-value "gardener" goal, you can pick a "panda" goal (they usually have a lower average value) and exploit the pursuit of the first goal to make some progress in the pursuit of the second one.

Moreover, the differences in the average difficulty and value of each category of goals means that you have to keep an eye on your competitors more than I did in my first matches: the game can become a rush to goal completion or proceed slowly towards tougher and more rewarding goals and you must pay attention or you'll get it wrong.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
So, this is the first game that I have to rate on two different areas. 1) the game components - WOW, WOW, WOW!!!! This game is perfection. The box is lovely and the insert fits everything snugly. The tiles are beautiful, thick and chunky sized. The bamboo is colorful, amazing quality, and fit together perfectly. The cards are adequate and easy to distinguish. The panda and the farmer?! Seriously, these could not be cuter or well made. Just a lovely game.
2) The game - It's more zen than game. The game comes down to luck of the draw. Your opponent's objective cards are secret, so there really is no way to stop them scoring (unless you can guess what they are trying to do; difficult at best as the objective cards are so quick to accomplish). This game isn't just luck driven; it really does just plays itself. You just build a garden, albeit a beautiful one, draw some objective cards, and hopefully you win!
Usually, I would really dislike a game like this. However, it is really a relaxing experience. I could see this being loved by kids, very, very non-gamers, and gamers just wanting to play filler to completely chill-out. This is game is like appreciating a traditional Chinese garden (which the games artwork mimics well).

The game's easy enough to get into, has a nice luck to strategy ratio and is engaging for both kids and adults to play. Absolutely recommend it.

RATING: 6.5
BGG

Charming wee game that's fun to play light heartedly with the ones you love.

Ultimately, the winner is most likely to be decided based upon other factors rather than a player's own decision making. What cards you draw, what the die lands on and what your opponents do matters more that what you do.

It is what it is - so lots of charm, luck and chaos - perfect for it's target audience (Gateway weight Gamers and families). Everyone else would be best to avoid it in favour of less charming games.

RATING: 8
I must admit I had to be persuaded to play Takenoko, it just did not look like my type of game, but looks can be deceiving. It is a relatively short game, not a "filler" but at the same time it does not hit that wall of "this is taking too long". I am a player who does not, on average, tolerate a game lasting more than an hour or at most an hour and a half, however in the cases of these games going long (which is not usual) I still don't get that restless feeling. This is a GREAT gateway game and I even play with my 8 year old, but at the same time my eldest son, 16 yr old, loves playing too. It is a good strategy game with some good visuals and tactics. TRY IT! 8/10

RATING: 2
Very nice components, but I don't see much beyond that. Dice rolls determine which of the unbalanced bonus options you get. There's a modicum of strategy in drawing cards as much as possible to maximize your point-scoring options early, but the hand limit cuts this off quickly, and once the board develops, the card draws result in ridiculous swings in points at the end of the game. Ultimately, it's following instructions and hoping to get lucky; I don't see much "game" here.

NOTE: I think we missed the rule about discarding mission cards that are already fulfilled upon drawing them. That makes the endgame swings less likely, so I might be willing to try this again.

RATING: 8
Takenoko is a wonderful light strategy game.  It has a reputation for being too random (with regard to randomly drawn objectives), but this is actually a learning-curve problem.  If inexperienced players start indiscriminately growing bamboo, the balance gets thrown off and the game becomes about who has the best objective cards.  If players are strategic about panda placement and bamboo growth, the game is interesting & tense. Growing Bamboo is like choosing craftsman in Puerto Rico.

RATING: 8
Takenoko hat nicht nur eine super niedliche Aufmachung und tolles Spielmaterial, dahinter versteckt sich auch noch ein richtig schönes Familienspiel. Die Regeln sind schnell erklärt und der Einstieg leicht. Trotzdem bietet Takenko mit unterschiedlichen Aktionsmöglichkeiten und den vielen Aufgabenkarten eine menge Optionen und Strategien.
